Each layer has specific responsibilities in validating, processing, and persisting the Deployment object.\\n\\n## Layer 1: Client Library (sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go)\\n\\n### Entry Point: DeploymentInterface\\n\\nThe journey begins in the Go client library at `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go`, where the `DeploymentInterface` defines the public API. This interface exposes the `Create` method that users call to create Deployments:\\n\\n```go\\nCreate(ctx context.Context, deployment *appsv1.Deployment, opts metav1.CreateOptions) (*appsv1.Deployment, error)\\n```\\n\\n### HTTP Request Construction: Client[T].Create\\n\\nThe actual implementation is a generic client in `gentype/type.go` that implements `Create` using Go generics. When invoked, the `Client[T].Create` method:\\n\\n1. Prepares the REST request using the HTTP POST method\\n2. Constructs the URL path: `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments`\\n3. Deserializes the server response back into a Deployment object\\n\\nThis design uses Go generics to provide a reusable client for any Kubernetes resource type without code duplication.\\n\\n## Layer 2: Kubernetes API Server (kubernetes/kubernetes)\\n\\n### HTTP Handler: createHandler\\n\\nWhen the HTTP request arrives at the Kubernetes API server, it is routed to the `createHandler` function in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`. This is a generic storage handler used by all Kubernetes resources. The `Store.Create` method:\\n\\n1. Calls the underlying storage backend's `Create` method with a storage key and the serialized object\\n\\n### Deployment-Specific Configuration: DeploymentStorage\\n\\nThe API server's deployment storage in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go` registers the Deployment REST handler. The `DeploymentStorage` type contains the `REST` field, which embeds the generic `Store` with deployment-specific configuration:\\n\\n- **CreateStrategy**: Uses `deployment.Strategy` to define validation and preparation logic\\n- **Storage key pattern**: `deployments.apps` in etcd (scoped to namespace if applicable)\\n- **Subresources**: Also exposes `/status`, `/scale`, and `/rollback` endpoints\\n\\n## Layer 3: etcd Storage (etcd-io/etcd)\\n\\n### API Handler: applierV3backend.Put\\n\\nOnce the Kubernetes API server has validated the Deployment, it calls the storage backend's `Create` method, which ultimately results in a Put request to etcd. Delegates to the MVCC transaction layer\\n\\n### Transaction Layer: storeTxnWrite.put\\n\\nThe core MVCC transaction handler in `server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go` (the `storeTxnWrite.put` method):\\n\\n1. Handles lease attachment for time-based expiration (if configured)\\n4. Calls `UnsafeSeqPut` to persist the data to the storage backend\\n5. Updates the in-memory B+ tree index for efficient lookups\\n\\n### Low-Level Storage: batchTx.unsafePut\\n\\nThe `batchTx.unsafePut` function in `server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go`:\\n\\n1. Retrieves the appropriate BoltDB bucket (collections like \\\"key\\\" for KV data)\\n2. Sets FillPercent=0.9 for sequential append-only optimization\\n3. Calls `bucket.Put(key, value)` to write the marshaled Deployment to the embedded BoltDB store\\n4. Buffers the write in a transaction (not yet persisted to disk)\\n\\n### Durability: batchTx.commit\\n\\nFinally, the `batchTx.commit` function ensures durability:\\n\\n1. Calls `tx.Commit()` on the BoltDB transaction\\n2. Writes all buffered changes to the memory-mapped BoltDB file\\n3. BoltDB handles the actual disk I/O through its B+ tree structure\\n4. Increments metrics for monitoring and debugging\\n\\n## Complete Request Flow\\n\\n```\\nClient Application\\n  ↓\\nDeploymentInterface.Create() [client-go/kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go]\\n store\\n```\\n\\n## Key Design Principles\\n\\n1. **Separation of Concerns**: The client library handles HTTP communication, the API server handles validation and authorization, and etcd handles persistence.\\n\\n2. **Generic Architecture**: Both the Kubernetes API server and the Go client use generics to provide reusable implementations for all resource types (not just Deployments).\\n\\n3. **Transaction Safety**: etcd uses MVCC (Multi-Version Concurrency Control) to ensure consistency and handle concurrent operations.\\n\\n4. **Buffered Writes**: etcd batches writes and flushes them
